data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300" /> -60.8%</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Source:<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Rome\xe2\x80\x93Fiumicino International Airport "Leonardo da Vinci"</b> (<a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <i lang="it">Aeroporto Internazionale di Roma&#8211;Fiumicino "Leonardo da Vinci"</i>; <a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>FCO</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>LIRF</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a> and the major airport in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.  It is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">busiest airports in Europe by passenger traffic</a> with over 43.5 million passengers served in 2019.\n</p><p>The airport serves as the main <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a> for <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a>, the largest Italian <a href="/wiki/Airline" title="Airline">airline</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vueling" title="Vueling">Vueling</a>, a Spanish <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carrier</a> owned by <a href="/wiki/International_Airlines_Group" title="International Airlines Group">International Airlines Group</a>.  Based on total passenger numbers, it is the eighth-busiest airport in Europe and was the world\'s <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by passenger traffic">47th-busiest airport</a> in 2017. It covers an area of 16&#160;km<sup>2</sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and is named after <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">polymath</a> <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> who, in 1480, designed a flying machine with wings and the first proto <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">helicopter</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" accidents</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>During construction the remains of <a href="/wiki/Caligula%27s_Giant_Ship" title="Caligula&#39;s Giant Ship">Caligula\'s Giant Ship</a> were found.\n</p><p>The airport was officially opened on 15 January 1961, with two <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a>, replacing the smaller <a href="/wiki/Rome_Ciampino_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rome Ciampino Airport">Rome Ciampino Airport</a>, which remains in service for some low-cost airlines as well as domestic and charter operations.  Despite being officially opened in 1961, Leonardo da Vinci\xe2\x80\x93Fiumicino Airport had actually been in use since 20 August 1960.  This was to help relieve air traffic that was congesting Rome Ciampino Airport during the <a href="/wiki/1960_Summer_Olympics" title="1960 Summer Olympics">1960 Summer Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 1960s, home-carrier Alitalia invested heavily in the new airport, building hangars and maintenance centres; in the same period a third runway was added (16L/34R).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_development">Later development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Later development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Security Services transferred from the <a href="/wiki/Polizia_di_Stato" title="Polizia di Stato">Polizia di Stato</a> (Italian State Police) to Aeroporti di Roma S.p.A. in 2000. Aeroporti di Roma created ADR Security S.r.l. (100%-owned) to provide these services as well as security services to airlines (in competition with other security companies such as IVRI).  Airport Security is supervised by Polizia di Stato, <a href="/wiki/Guardia_di_Finanza" title="Guardia di Finanza">Guardia di Finanza</a> (Italian Customs Police), <a href="/wiki/Italian_Civil_Aviation_Authority" title="Italian Civil Aviation Authority">Italian Civil Aviation Authority</a> and Aeroporti di Roma S.p.A..<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Ground handling services were provided by Aeroporti di Roma until 1999, when it created Aeroporti di Roma Handling (to serve all airlines except for <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a>, which continued to be handled by Aeroporti di Roma itself). Alitalia provided passenger assistance even before 1999. In 2001, Alitalia created "Alitalia Airport" and started providing ground handling for itself and other airlines. Aeroporti di Roma Handling remains the biggest handler in terms of airlines handled, but Alitalia Airport is the biggest handler in terms of airplanes handled as Alitalia aircraft account for 50% of the ones at Fiumicino. In May 2006, Italy\'s Civil Aviation Authority announced that it took off the limitation of 3 ramp handlers in Rome Leonardo da Vinci airport. ARE Group and <a href="/wiki/Aviapartner" title="Aviapartner">Aviapartner</a> announced that they would create a company called Aviapartner (51% Aviapartner; 49% ARE Group) to serve Milan Malpensa and Rome Leonardo da Vinci.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Since 2005, the airport operates a <a href="/wiki/Category_III_approach" class="mw-redirect" title="Category III approach">category III B</a> <a href="/wiki/Instrument_landing_system" title="Instrument landing system">instrument landing system</a> (ILS). Further improvement work was implemented in 2007 to enable the airport to handle 30 <a href="/wiki/Takeoff" title="Takeoff">takeoffs</a>/<a href="/wiki/Landing" title="Landing">landings</a> per hour, up from 10, in the event of thick fog. Three runways presently operate at Leonardo da Vinci airport: 16L/34R and 16R/34L (separated by a distance of 4,000&#160;m (13,000&#160;ft), and 07/25, used only westwards for takeoffs owing to the prevailing winds. The airport used to have a fourth runway, 16C/34C which was located alongside 16L/34R, it was mostly used as a taxiway or as a backup for 16L/34R; the runway is now designated as Taxiway "D".<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010, the new single <a href="/wiki/Baggage_handling_system" title="Baggage handling system">baggage handling system</a> for more efficient luggage delivery began operations.\n</p><p>Several projects are planned. These include the construction of an environmentally-friendly <a href="/wiki/Cogeneration" title="Cogeneration">cogeneration</a> system, which would allow the airport to produce its own energy; construction of Pier C (dedicated to international flights) with 16 additional loading bridges, to handle the expected growth from 38 million passengers per year in 2014 to 55 million by 2018; and the "Masterplan Fiumicino Nord", involving four new terminals and two new runways to be built in the future handling 100 million passengers per year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport currently features three <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">passenger terminals</a>, of which two are operational.\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Terminal 1</b> (Gates <i>B1\xe2\x80\x93B30</i>) is used by <a href="/wiki/Alitalia" title="Alitalia">Alitalia</a> and other <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> airlines.</li>\n<li><b>Terminal 3</b> (Gates <i>C8\xe2\x80\x93C16</i>, <i>D1\xe2\x80\x93D10</i>, <i>E1-E8</i>, <i>E11-E24</i>, <i>E31-44</i> and <i>E51-61</i>) is the largest terminal which is used by most of the companies.</li>\n<li><b>Terminal 5 (under refurbishment)</b> (formerly Gates <i>E1-E8</i>, <i>E11-E24</i>, <i>E31-44</i> and <i>E51-61</i>) was used by all U.S. and Israeli carriers. This terminal is currently closed for extensive renovation.<sup id="cite_ref-adr.it_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adr.it-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The terminals were upgraded during the 1990s and 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 1991, the domestic Pier A with 12 gates opened, followed in 1995 by the international Pier B with 10 gates and in 1999 by the international Satellite C with 14 gates. In 2000, the new domestic Terminal A opened, and the terminal buildings, then consisting of Terminal A (with Pier A), Terminal AA, Terminal B (with Pier B) and Terminal C (with Satellite C), were reorganized.\n</p><p>The dedicated <a href="/wiki/Air_freight" class="mw-redirect" title="Air freight">Cargo City</a> terminal was added in 2004, while the check-in counters for American carriers and <a href="/wiki/El_Al" title="El Al">El Al</a> in Terminal 5 opened in 2008, with passengers then being <a href="/wiki/Airport_bus" title="Airport bus">bused</a> to what was then called Satellite C. In 2009, the terminals were renamed \xe2\x80\x93 A was renamed T1, AA was renamed T2, B and C became T3, and T5 stayed the same.  The former Terminal 2 closed permanently on 15 December 2017 to make way for the expansion of Terminal 1.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="SkyBridge">SkyBridge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: SkyBridge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>An automated <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">people mover</a> (APM) called <b>SkyBridge</b> opened in 1999 along with the Satellite C. It consists of two stations, one in the third floor of Terminal 3, and the other in the second floor of gate area E31-44. This <a href="/wiki/Shuttle_train" title="Shuttle train">shuttle train</a> is the only means of transport for passengers between the two parts of the terminal. The westbound service, from T3 to Gates E31-44, is for departing passengers only, while the eastbound service is for arriving passengers only. Arriving passengers are not permitted to take the train back, as they need to pass through a transfer <a href="/wiki/Security_checkpoint" title="Security checkpoint">security checkpoint</a> to reenter the departure area. Likewise, departing passengers are not permitted to take the train back to Terminal 3.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled, seasonal and charter flights to and from Fiumicino:<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a Transat</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</center>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transportation">Ground transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Ground transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fiumicino_Aeroporto_railway_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Fiumicino_Aeroporto_railway_station.jpg/220px-Fiumicino_Aeroporto_railway_station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Fiumicino_Aeroporto_railway_station.jpg/330px-Fiumicino_Aeroporto_railway_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Fiumicino_Aeroporto_railway_station.jpg/440px-Fiumicino_Aeroporto_railway_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fiumicino_Aeroporto_railway_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fiumicino_Aeroporto_railway_station" title="Fiumicino Aeroporto railway station">Fiumicino Aeroporto railway station</a></div></div></div>\n<table class="infobox" style="width:25em;"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above" style="border-top: 4px solid #000080; border-bottom: 4px solid #000080;">SkyBridge</th></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #efefef;">Overview</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Status</th><td class="infobox-data">Operational</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Owner</th><td class="infobox-data">Aeroporti di Roma</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Locale</th><td class="infobox-data">Leonardo da Vinci\xe2\x80\x93Fiumicino Airport, Italy</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Stations</th><td class="infobox-data">2</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #efefef;">Service</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Type</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">People mover</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Services</th><td class="infobox-data">1</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Rolling stock</th><td class="infobox-data">2 <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Innovia_APM_100" title="Bombardier Innovia APM 100">Bombardier Innovia APM 100</a> vehicles</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #efefef;">History</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Track length</th><td class="infobox-data">0.55 km</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Character</th><td class="infobox-data">Serves sterile parts of the airport</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Train">Train</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Train">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Fiumicino_Aeroporto_railway_station" title="Fiumicino Aeroporto railway station">Fiumicino Aeroporto railway station</a> is served by the <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_Express" title="Leonardo Express">Leonardo Express</a> train operated by <a href="/wiki/Trenitalia" title="Trenitalia">Trenitalia</a>, available at the airport terminal. It takes 30 minutes to get to <a href="/wiki/Roma_Termini_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Roma Termini station">Termini Station</a> in a non-stop trip that is provided every 15 minutes. Alternatively, local trains (FL1 line) leave once every 15 minutes, stopping at all stations. However, these trains do not head to Termini station. Passengers have to change at <a href="/wiki/Roma_Trastevere_railway_station" title="Roma Trastevere railway station">Trastevere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roma_Ostiense_railway_station" title="Roma Ostiense railway station">Ostiense</a> (<a href="/wiki/Piramide_(Rome_Metro)" title="Piramide (Rome Metro)">Metro Piramide</a>) or <a href="/wiki/Roma_Tuscolana_railway_station" title="Roma Tuscolana railway station">Tuscolana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The railway opened in December 1989, with nonstop and several stop services available.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Leonardo da Vinci is about 35&#160;km (22&#160;mi) by car from Rome\'s historic city centre. The airport is served by the six-lane <a href="/wiki/Autostrada_A91_(Italy)" title="Autostrada A91 (Italy)">Autostrada A91</a> motorway and numerous buses and taxis.\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>From the 1960s until the 1980s, the airport experienced significant <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_hijacking" title="Aircraft hijacking">aircraft hijackings</a> as well as being the scene of two major <a href="/wiki/List_of_terrorist_incidents" title="List of terrorist incidents">terrorist attacks</a> and the port of origin for an aircraft bombing in flight\xe2\x80\x94some engendered by Palestinians as part of the <a href="/wiki/Israeli%E2%80%93Palestinian_conflict" title="Israeli\xe2\x80\x93Palestinian conflict">Israeli\xe2\x80\x93Palestinian conflict</a>.\n</p>\n<ul><li>On 23 November 1964, <a href="/wiki/TWA_Flight_800_(1964)" title="TWA Flight 800 (1964)">TWA Flight 800</a>, operated by a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">Boeing 707</a>, had an engine catch fire during takeoff. 50 of the 73 passengers and crew on board were killed.</li>\n<li>On 17 December 1973, during the <a href="/wiki/1973_Rome_airport_attacks_and_hijacking" title="1973 Rome airport attacks and hijacking">1973 Rome airport attacks and hijacking</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707-321B" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 707-321B">Boeing 707-321B</a> operating as <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan American World Airways</a> (Pan Am) Flight 110 was attacked by Palestinian assailants. 30 passengers were killed when <a href="/wiki/White_phosphorus_(weapon)" class="mw-redirect" title="White phosphorus (weapon)">phosphorus bombs</a> were thrown aboard the aircraft as it was preparing for departure.<sup id="cite_ref-fgarch-rome-dec73_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fgarch-rome-dec73-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> During the same incident a <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a> <span class="nowrap">(D-ABEY)</span><sup id="cite_ref-asn-dec73_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asn-dec73-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> was hijacked and landed at Athens, Damascus and finally in Kuwait. All remaining passengers and crew were then released.<sup id="cite_ref-fgarch-rome-dec73_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fgarch-rome-dec73-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> One person died in the incident.<sup id="cite_ref-asn-dec73_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asn-dec73-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 27 December 1985, during the <a href="/wiki/Rome_and_Vienna_airport_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="Rome and Vienna airport attacks">Rome and Vienna airport attacks</a>, assailants shot and killed 16 people and wounded 99 others at the airport.</li>\n<li>On 17 October 1988, <a href="/wiki/Uganda_Airlines_Flight_775" title="Uganda Airlines Flight 775">Uganda Airlines Flight 775</a> from <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">London Gatwick</a> to <a href="/wiki/Entebbe_International_Airport" title="Entebbe International Airport">Entebbe International Airport</a> via Fiumicino, crashed short of the runway after two missed approaches. Twenty-six of the 45 passengers aboard, as well as all 7 crew members, died.</li>\n<li>On 2 February 2013, Alitalia Flight 1670, operated by a leased <a href="/wiki/ATR_72" title="ATR 72">ATR 72</a>, en route from <a href="/wiki/Pisa_International_Airport" title="Pisa International Airport">Pisa International Airport</a> to Rome, overran the runway during landing. Sixteen occupants were injured, two of them seriously.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-foxcrawl_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxcrawl-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The aircraft was subsequently written off.</li>\n<li>On 8 June 2013, Wizz Air Flight 3141, an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320-232" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320-232">Airbus A320-232</a>(registration HA-LWM) from <a href="/wiki/Henri_Coand%C4%83_International_Airport" title="Henri Coand\xc4\x83 International Airport">Bucharest - Henri Coand\xc4\x83 Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> to <a href="/wiki/Ciampino%E2%80%93G._B._Pastine_International_Airport" title="Ciampino\xe2\x80\x93G. B. Pastine International Airport">Rome-Ciampino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, made an emergency landing at <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Fiumicino Airport</a> when the crew encountered problems lowering one of the main <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">undercarriages</a> and locking it into position. The aircraft diverted to Fiumicino because of the longer runway, and firefighters applied foam after landing as a precautionary measure. The aircraft was evacuated using slides. Initial reports of injured passengers were denied by both Wizz Air and Rome Fiumicino Airport, who said some passengers requested medical checkups but reported no injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 29 September 2013 at 20:10, an Alitalia <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A320" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A320">Airbus A320</a> flying from <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Barajas_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Madrid Barajas Airport">Madrid Barajas Airport</a> to <a href="/wiki/Rome_Fiumicino_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Rome Fiumicino Airport">Rome Fiumicino Airport</a> failed to deploy the <a href="/wiki/Landing_gear" title="Landing gear">landing gear</a> during a storm on landing and the aircraft toppled, skidded off the runway, and crashed. Ten passengers suffered minor injuries, and all 151 passengers and crew were evacuated and taken to hospital.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardo_da_Vinci%E2%80%93Fiumicino_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section:
